des hermofrodites	The text appears to be discussing a medical or surgical procedure related to hermaphrodites (individuals with physical characteristics that do not fit typical male or female norms).
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaproditism is according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles appears as well as the shape of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes in court the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has above the navel as well as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment of a boil and a pustule is that you cut out the gathered pus, and treat it like other wounds. In the second manner, for men whose urine runs through the skin of their groin, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tendon (or possibly "ligament")
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The carbuncle is a gathered pus above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have had one as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must mark the superfluity of the carbuncle to your hand or fingers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deeply in, lest there be an outpouring of blood, then treat it with another treatment until you are cured; and for a boil that arises at the mouth of the anus, and swells, and perhaps bursts, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and because of this they called it the ancient "cow sickness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cover it, as we have said of the incision, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	This appears to be an old French medical term that might refer to a type of skin condition or imperfection, possibly related to the concept of "erratic" in modern English (meaning irregular or unpredictable). However, without more context, it's difficult to provide a precise definition. Can you give me more information or explain where this term is from?
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratique if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pores are small; and it is natural by birth, or occurs by accident from disease that has come to it; or it is caused by accumulated fat, or subtle or thick sap, and it is formed in front, or in sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is nearby appearances, it should be touched with your hands or with oil.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is subtle sap and it is nearby the two kidneys, if you hurry, and sew in: put your two fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then press the two kidneys firmly, until the subtle sap is stopped, and the swelling goes away; then take linen, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman lie at home each day, so that she cannot join.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scab is hard and thick, you must scrape off the crust like the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from pus, suspend it to the incision and scrape it off; and have blood-stopping medicines, as sage, dragon's blood, frankincense, along with plenty of egg; then bind a cloth bandage that is wide enough so that the wound cannot close itself; thus be long-lasting, and give him a linen tent that is dry; then you cure him with other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there comes pus in the marrow, it must be scraped off in this manner, unless it is an inflamed abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For at an inflamed abscess that is in the marrow, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Haemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Venereal sores are openings of veins that normally seep without a scab, and when venereal sores are old they become ulcers; and we have already said in the division the likenesses to them, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I declare that hemorrhoids and a thrombus, when they are deep within the rectum, and do not appear to the touch, should not be treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the opening of the rectum, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You should then put the woman in a cold house, and heat an awl or iron on the tongs, and sear it on her roots, then sprinkle medicines constricting blood, such as cypress and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to a wooden beam for one hour, then put her in cold water; and if she bleeds a lot, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and lily, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he remains steady, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him have cupping glasses on the back and shoulders without hurting them; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess settles, then heal the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a sharp head, so you must cover it as I said about the boil; and then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Je vois que vous avez identifié le texte comme étant une description d'apostèmes (ou hémorroïdes) de la marris (apparemment un terme ancien pour désigner l'intérieur des fesses ou les canaux analiens).
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the groin, such as ulcers and septic abscesses and herpetic eruptions and carbuncles and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that collect pus; and if you wish to know how to work with iron, then look and see if the abscess is swollen at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce at once, but let it cools down as long as the pain is alleviated; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats that he leans against, and support him on his back and bring his feet towards the parts behind the leg; and let his thighs be spread wide, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good cord; then stretch out the belly towards the right side, and bring in the instrument with which one works at the mouth of the groin from which this form comes later; and it is necessary that when you see to introduce this instrument, you place the first nail in place so as to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and do not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument above, and holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess appears, and one makes it soft with the hand, then it must be covered at the head with a bandage of linen clean and moist in water or herbs that have been cooked; and put the tent far from the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and put on top of the marrow and on the point of the elbow a bandage of linen clean and moist in vinegar or leaves that have been cooked; then cure it after two days of ointment according to what is suitable for those things, until they are healed; and sometimes lift up the marrow and the wound by washing with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and long aristolochus that have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is returned in the marrow, then you must be careful not to cook with iron, but heal it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first at the bedside that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are such that when you see the woman advance below, and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to force its issue; therefore know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and it comes out under her head, and the second son with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it descends above her head, the second son comes with him, and there is a cleansing of its superfluities by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens at times that it comes out above its feet, and forces its way out of the body through the legs, or the thighs, or the hands; or it comes out above her belly, or sometimes it is converted by chance onto his neck, and by other bad figures; it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures about how one should aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out under its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth easily, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a birthing stool, where women usually sit; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then give the midwife a small spatula in the form of:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and rend the placenta, and scrape with a finger as far as the moisture that is inside it flows; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman must be cleansed with fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her feel and bear down with conditio, and keep her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then you must gently ease them in and out; and if they cannot enter, then lift the woman onto a seat, and raise her feet up high; then tip the seat back down to the ground, and restrain the woman so she does not fall over; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child is dead, then take hold of the hands with the knife that was placed before, and pull out the child, and ease them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	The issue of the child from its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the infant comes onto its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards; and then turn it slowly little by little until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it cries out just to the hips, then command that it be held back, and let it stop crying; if it cries out loudly, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't kick further than what we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light. (meaning: the umbilical cord is no longer attached and the child can now be safely removed)
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take alum, and oil of sassafras, and gum dissolved, and grind all together in a mortar; and put on the natural substance of woman inside and above this ointment, then make her sit in a heated bath down to the hip bones; and when she is moistened below, then make the girdle of myrrh, and put it below, and leave her an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then let her cry out and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly touch her belly, for the infant now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child from its thighs (or possibly "legs")
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, so put the pillow under his hands small and small; then be placed on his neck, and hang his legs down, and lie thus on the bed; and bend his hands small and small, and then take hold of his hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is prepared to go down; and if the infant does not jump, take his feet and straighten him out, then move the belly up, then put your hands in; and squeeze the infant small and small; and command the woman to take hold of herself as long as the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child which comes out with one hand open wide (meaning: the baby's arm is extended as it emerges from the birth canal)
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to instruct the woman to bring back her hand: if she cannot bring it back, make her get up and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed and straighten out her legs; then administer the medicament that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and squeeze the infant according to its natural shape, and cause it to be expelled, and command her to take hold of herself as long as the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child on its back, with its hands spread out and its face turned towards its mother's back. (meaning: the baby has been born and is lying on its mother's chest)

It is necessary that the patient let their hand rest on top of a heated stone or ball, then turn it slowly and lightly; and when it is even, so place upon it a natural mustard made with ale and oil, as we have said, then instruct them to move it slowly; and when you have done this, so make them sit on the seat, and instruct them to grasp it; and they must hold still.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by the same manner for the entire afterbirth. (meaning: the instructions given by the midwife should be followed in the same way for all parts of the afterbirth, such as any remaining tissue or placenta)
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to the second stage in this manner, so crush the afterbirth with your nail, until the moisture is drained; and if the navel of the child and its neck are swollen, then crush it from below, that it be not retained, and kill the child; then put the baby inside, as long as you have put it in the way it should be, and instruct the woman to grasp herself once: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even triplets or quadruplets are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are an extraordinary thing, and do not live at all, if one can give them a name; I know these, that they multiply greatly, and are severed by the womb which conceives them, which is linked to the belly; and sometimes issue naturally like us all, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue suddenly, then the cure is as we have said, and the belly is subtle, and does quickly and lightly what it makes; and do thusly as one would move towards health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen times, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of its age glorious, and it is fitting that the belly knows all these things, because similar things might happen to him; so do as seems necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman after a dead or stillborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform hands-on work; so it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of good health, and has no accident or fear of death; so it is necessary that the woman be covered on her back, and her shoulders inclined downwards, and her legs lifted; and a minister should sprinkle two parts of the powder, or she should be tied to the bed if she cannot be treated at the descent of the child; then rub the mouth with moist oil mixed with marigold and fenugreek seed and flaxseed, then anoint the hands of the midwife with these oils and sediments; then put them in the woman lightly, then look for the ligatures that are suitable for this purpose, and take care if the child is apparent it will descend on its head; so tie the ligatures in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the groin or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, tie them at the cost of the ankles; and it is necessary that you sprinkle the ligature with your right hand, and put the crown between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the ligature into any of these places that we have said, until it comes to an empty thing; and this is the shape of the ligature:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then bind it against another bandage, or the third one if you need to, so that the extractions are equal; and then stretch them equally in moving from one side and the other, for movement to come out, and the bandages should be dentated so as to hold, as is this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if one part remains, then anoint the ball with some of his oils, and put them in that part, and draw the other part; and if there remains not at all, then place this bandage or a higher position, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back for lack of holding, then you must wrap a cloth over it, so that it comes out completely; then tie at the joint of the wrist or at the elbow, and similarly do to the other hand, and to both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's joint is thick and he is stretched at the exit, or he has a sharp chief assembled, you must push the spatula spine between your fingers, and make the chief and extract the sharp point; or use the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and do the same for him if the child has a natural large joint; and then draw out the bones in forceps, and if the joint jumps out and holds at the strong point, it may be split, until the moistor which is in the lower exit comes out; and if it cannot come out, you must break by pieces on the nail that you have; and if it is swollen in the stomach or under the ribs, you must make a hole as much as the moistor flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the extraction is light and the approach to the mouth of the womb is easy. (meaning: in this situation, the delivery process is straightforward and uncomplicated, with the baby being born in a normal position and the umbilical cord presenting itself for removal)
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is stretched in the stomach or belly, you must draw it out to the cloth wrapped around the hand; and make the stomach or belly, as much as the moistor that is there flows; and if other members are removed, and the joint remains, place the staff's handle on top of the navel, and pull it until the mouth of the navel opens; then put in the thread or string, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the navel is constricted due to hot abscess that has come there, you must not trouble yourself, but rather use moist and greasy things; and apply ointments, and mix with soft water and soothing liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is above its side, and you can make it even, so administer what we have said for a living child; and if you cannot, then cut it through with pieces, and leave nothing of the membranes.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, administer what we have said for hot swellings that come in the groin; and if there is bleeding from pus, it should be placed in a narrow stream, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a dead child had been, then she conceived another on top of that one and rejected the death of the other. (meaning: the woman was pregnant with a stillborn fetus, but became pregnant again shortly after, and her body somehow managed to reject or expel the stillborn fetus)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time the came warm afterbirths in the belly, and swelled so much that they burst open, and began to rot greatly. (meaning: the woman's body was experiencing severe complications, including the formation of multiple warm afterbirths, which were causing her abdomen to swell significantly and eventually rupture)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound. (meaning: the midwife was summoned to assist with the delivery and complications that were occurring, but despite her efforts, she was unable to stop the bleeding or repair the damage to the mother's body)
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong attracting ointment, and came out a bone, and after some days another. (meaning: the midwife applied a powerful medicinal paste to try and stop the bleeding, but instead of resolving the issue, it caused more bones from the mother's body to be released)
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very astonished, because the belly has no bone. (meaning: the midwife was shocked and amazed that the mother's body was releasing bones, which is not a normal or expected part of the delivery process)
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child. (meaning: based on her experience and knowledge, the midwife believed that the bones being released were from a fetus that had died in utero)
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I sewed the wound, and with a few bones I guided the woman to better position; and the woman survived long in this way, and she quickly returned to good health from the bone; and I have no record of this chapter being otherwise except that, when the master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the womb to its place. (meaning: the final step, after resolving all complications, is to return the mother's body to its normal state and position)
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	This after comes the shape of the presseur, by which we write the books; and two turns with two hands to the two feet of the two patients. (meaning: the text is describing a tool or instrument called "pressor", which is used for writing or recording information, and also references the process of turning pages in a book)
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the pincer should be more subtle than the retractor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the opening of the handle should be two finger-widths wide, and the edge of the trees one and a half palms long; and between the two levers there should be two fastenings of the same wood, which are firm in both, half a palm long or a little more; and these two fastenings are inserted into the mouth of the groin to open it when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, is made from ebony wood or boxwood, according to the shape of pincers; and has two springs, as you see, one palm long and one finger wide; and when you open the container completely with all the instrument, have the woman sit on the bed with her feet apart and legs open; then insert the two springs together into the container, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand over all the instrument, as you did with the pincers equally, according to the size that you see opening the mouth of the container, until the handle makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and their similarities multiplied; and when the craftsmen have prepared them, then is the work more hurried and men reach greater heights because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	You should not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then have her strain with effort, and grasp your hands at the mouth and navel; and if she falls for this reason, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the apple of gall, and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the abscess, such as wormwood, rue, anise, chamomile, sassafras, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or put in water on the fire; then put a cord or hole into the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the abscess, and make it steam until the vapors come inside the abscess; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this cure and is not healed, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or muskellunge gall, and then put it into nature, and wait for the second day; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it little by little straight out, so that the abscess does not break during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pulled out; and if it comes and discharges.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the mareis is tightly constricted, we have said the cure for hiccoughing and fumigation with herbs; and if she does not recover from all that we have said, be sure to do nothing more; but it is necessary to tie what is at the mouth of the mareis to the navel of the woman, then purge her with triple ointment; if she will pass it and come back, and become feverish; but however, when she passes, an evil odor comes into the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is therefore fitting to do purifying fumigations with it; no ancient has experimented with fumigation of sorrel and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at the retention of flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to see something similar to a cord, and one puts the head finely into its nature, and the hives wide on fire; and let there be fumigations above the coals, and the itch until it is consumed, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation ( likely referring to a medical procedure)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but it is stopped with a small sponge: so then at the well it should be that the woman pierces this sponge to its due measure, and does not let the lancet pierce too deeply or hurt the ligament; then put on moist linen in vinegar and oil, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close over again, then put or pierce a piece of linen into the fundament, and leave it in for a long time, and have it taken out when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at any time this stoppage comes to be sudden from a cut or an abscess; then it is fitting to cover that suddenness: if it is healed, if as we have said of the linen sponge.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the fundament (likely referring to an abnormal connection or tunnel between two organs or structures)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that come from under the fundament are nodation, and grow larger than those that come from under the fundament of the back; or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more. And when this nodation is ancient, it operates, and draws more moisture than a white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and are known by the excretion or vomiting or fetidness when the patient makes an emesis, and perhaps a springing up of worms.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just up to the bladder, and just up to half of the penis; and reach just up to the groin, and just not into the rectum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the persisting fistula under the fundament and not persisting; and it is that you press with your first finger or fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twistiness, you insert a thin thread of linen or horsehair into the fistula until you feel the thread or hair with your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no discharge or vomiting or worm, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is present just to the bladder or just to the urine duct, then the urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just up to the joint of the thigh, then the tendon comes back to its place; if there is no twist and the invention of pain around it, then it is that he goes badly, and there is no medicine nor salve by anointing; and in these piercing fistulas there is not a true cure except labor, and vanity of foolish wise men who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not pierced and is not old, there is hope of health by iron, as I have tried, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and bend his thighs towards his belly; then insert a tent of lead, or of linen if there is twist, until you know where the tendon comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your index fingers there, if then you feel that the tendon is pierced; and when you sense between your finger and the fatty tissue or flesh, then know that it is pierced; if not trouble, then one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	On can treat some people well, but it happens seldom; and the help that one gives there, is to cauterize the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before; and put it all hot in the fistula, until it comes close to the bottom; and do this two or three times, until you know that those charred marks are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then cure with damp cloths in a burrow, until those charred marks ooze out; and then cure with ointment inflaming flesh and congealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus cured, it's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it can't be cured otherwise; and if the pus bursts in and doesn't pierce just to the bottom which is on the foundation, and between your skin and the pus there is a thick covering of flesh or scab, and you see the fistula at those that ensue the covering from the heat; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and push it ahead of the pus, and then cauterize afterwards, until it comes to the top of the pus; and the pus will be delivered, and will dry up; then scrape off those charred marks which resemble a bird's feather, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound swells and becomes inflamed between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal potion.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the fire cauterizes two things together: that is to say, the joining of two connected bones, and the scorching of blood and the drying out of moisture; then the cure for moist tents in mud or in a hazelnut shell, until the place bleeds freely, and the charred bone issues into the bowels; then cure the wound with ointments soothing the sore flesh, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just near to the fundament of the fundament, and is far from the body, then insert a finger or a probe into it, and investigate further.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor and there are two layers or the skin or membrane or bone, where it is close to bursting, if there are no signs of hope and faith, through the administration of one of the three methods: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut into it just until the bottom, or if you can see, put tents in it and cure it as first; and do not go too deep, that you do not cut the inner lining which holds the foundation, and bring about an ejection without will: then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut near the foundation, by tent or other instrument designated; then wash out the bad bone that is in the wound, as long as you can; then try to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part away from the foundation: if this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time fistulas are formed in this manner: and it is when you plug the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side near the foundation above the skin, so take a threaded tent with a head shaped like this:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I insert one twisted thread into the other, and insert the iron band all around the thread in the fistula as far as it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is threaded inside the margin of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that perforation, so that you plug your own joint or foundation; and pull out the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and leave for one day or two; and hold it once more, until the threads bind those pieces that are between them, and protrude; then treat the wound until it is sutured and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then make it perforate in all ways that you can see, unless it is too far forward.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a perforation in a place that is too far forward, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiny spine from which the fistula is made is quite pointed on one side and truncated on the other, for this reason they do not protrude those that should not protrude, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the veins
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emories are according to two manners: or they are within the fundament, just like grain of resin, and there are small ones and great ones, and in court at once blood, and there is one or more, and they protrude from the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have a lot of moisture, and in court at once a drop of yellowish water or a drop of blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament is that you command the patient to urinate so as to clear the fundament, until it appears with a thread; if you hurry, and pick up the emory with tweezers, or hold it at your fingernail, then cut off its roots; and if the thread cannot hold because of its moistors, take it by the cloth, or by cotton, or by a piece of chamelot; and pull it out with your hands, then cut it off, and powder it over some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them just as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then purge the patient with a purgative biting and harsh to clean what is within the fundament so that it can come out openly; when the patient feels it, and if the thread is protruding from the fundament, then the cure is light; and it is that you pick up at your fingernail or with tweezers, and cut it off, then cure them just as we have said, until they are healed, and so that he avoids the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you prepare the stitches in this manner: take a twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread against the needle, and make sure they are of equal length; and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do this with all the others, and leave one end for the excess of blood; then put on a linen pad soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it on, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him be until he stops bleeding, and when they are cut off, cure them with ointment and other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the fundament (or anus)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness in the fundament, either by natural constriction or because the illness has been old and medicine is no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset the tip of a spear or at your finger the outer layer which does not let it get moist; then cure it until it is solid as it needs to be; and if it cannot become solid, then start the scraping again stronger than before, until it heals more, and is scabbed over; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from the fistula (or fist)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small imperfection found near the body, and they go very deep in it. And sometimes the frost finds them, and one feels them just like dead from numbness, and comes to all of the body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a wire from a goose feather, or a strong bird's quill, and put this thread on the numbness, so that the circles of red (or maybe "purple"?) encircle the numbness all around; then turn your hand with the entire wire until you surround the numbness entirely, and push it in deep, and extract the numbness from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that, then do what with a wire of iron or steel in this shape, and be subtle below and pull out above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers and press on it. And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is said in the book of cauterizing.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the purge (or cathartic)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purge of silver or gold, or molten lead, and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments, according to the manner in which they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that one prepares for the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the purge, both small and large, is a tube that is wide at the top, or the belly is connected in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a constriction or the belly is bound together, as you see it, and the head is pierced from inside; and on one side there are two openings, and on the other one; and the belly is wrapped with medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small openings, and between each opening there is a thread of space, then put in these openings a strong thread of twisted cord made into a figure like the number X or a cross; and assemble the belly so that it forms a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the poultice with oil or egg yolk or similar thing, then insert it gently; then tighten the bandage by its two hands together until it is completely tight, then remove the poultice, and raise the patient's legs to the hip, and if the medicine wants to come out, so let it go as much as it can; and if he sleeps all night, so it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge them in the illness of intestinal decoration, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until they are healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, so let the poultice be as subtle as for a child; and that is the form of the subtle poultice on which the skin will be strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the cure for wounds; now we will speak of the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and in what manner they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by stumbling of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, beware lest it be from a sliver of stone or similar things, and the skin is torn in all places and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hot aposteme: if so do cleanse it with cephalic remedy immediately, even though it may bleed from the wound, and the cleansing should be on the contrary side to the injured part; and have the patient replete with wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it will not clean, if the patient's meat is wasted, and does not drink wine, nor eat meat; and places on the wound, when hot aposteme comes, moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot aposteme, if you place on the wound, when it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been touched by air, powder that I will say about soon afterwards; and if the burn has altered it, if you place some ointments on it, until it be clean.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be joined together by stitches, then join them by suturing, just as I will say about belly wounds, with sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be open to the bone, and it bleeds and holds only by a thread, sew it up; then treat the wound with medicine and repair hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as cooked testicles and bread, also fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find skin rot, and it is not to the bone, sew up the rot completely, and throw out pus, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, cut it off, and since it cannot be stopped by medicines, tie off the artery; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you put on this powder that heals similarly to cauterization (or more likely, a type of salve or ointment) once the wound has been cleaned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and quicksilver three parts, and finely grind the powder, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it has dried well and joined with all its blood; and then tie it up tightly, and leave it untied if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make this powder with charcoal alone, when one has neither incense nor dragon's blood, but only after the wound has been cleaned by fire (cauterization).
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, just as it is, do not put on this powder at all; but put on some digested ointments or flour of barley made with water and honey, so that it oozes pus; then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound and it is small, then take it out with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between this and one of the head, but if the nerves or the artery of the neck are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a hernia, then do not do anything to cure it and do not put any constricting thing on it, because it hurts the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation with the brain, which is the highest member, but if the medicine is moist, such as chalybeate water in sweet water, and mixed with rosina oil, and cucumber water also in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie it with bandages, and care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and swollen with pus, then pierce or lower in place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes out, then tie it off, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the duct is guarded, by which the meat goes, then cut the jugular on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural shape; and then restrain it properly, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments of old recipes until they are healed; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, then scrape; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and let what you cannot have alone, so that the wound may rot, and be drained and covered with a scab; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has formed an abscess or fistula, then care for it as I've said in its chapter on fistulas.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the stab wound with a lancet or dagger.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.
