If it is a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there is windiness coming from the wound and the patient is unconscious: you will know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in the wound at the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not dry up inside, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton wool in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient sleep on top of the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that there will be no spasms, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor straining of the eyelids; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal the patient with tents and other treatments, as long as it is possible to be cured; and if it cannot heal and work, then know that there is an abscess; treat it in such a way as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision of a sword or dagger and it is simple, or worse on the front, then treat it with what is before; if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has splintered pieces in the bone, then clean the wound, and pull out any foreign bodies that are embedded; and if they are not embedded, then let the wound suppurate, for this will aid extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, make a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small; from a large wound intestines or the guts may sometimes burst out by which the introduction of them is hindered; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it's worse for a small wound than a big one, so therefore we put the intestines back in cold to cold, because they swell immediately when they feel the cold, thus going in more tightly, and so it's better for a middle-sized wound, so that's why we reset the intestine to its place rather than other two Also know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners: the two common stitches happen on the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of the wounds of the body and the two other stitches proper are common to other wounds; and notwithstanding they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestines has come out, and a thing is to be put back in, this is done by one of two manners: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or cloth in hot water and only wet, or cook in boiling water with cypress and spikenard, and rise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do it restraining, and be cautious that it does not burst to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil and scald the stitches, because through these the entrance is facilitated to a small thing; and if it cannot enter, make a small hole in the wound with an instrument like that used to cut off hemorrhoids; and the first treatment must be careful not to cut without great necessity there being; and this is the instrument for cutting: so incise inside in the hilt and outwardly no, and look here at the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump forth, so put it back again according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have power to do so, for that helps much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the part under the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part under the belly, then place the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly, so that the hurt part of the belly is higher than the other; and thus one must take care to do as I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, put what is on you, then take between your hands a lint or cloth that covers all the wound with its hand, and assemble the edges; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's largeness, then leave from the head of the wound a double space, and stick in a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce through both the keys of the skin with the two keys of the siphac, which is inside the skin beneath, until you make it pierce through that part, and assemble the two ends of the siphac together with the four [ends] together; then pull out a double thread around the needle in two parts, then assemble the two edges of the wound well together, and then leave a double space, and stick in another needle; then tie the end of the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do it with the needles as much as you need them until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be middling, between fine and coarse, for fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot well enter: therefore they must be middling; and it does not matter to stick the needles too far into the flesh and skin, that they may pierce and open the wound before the suturing; and then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient at night, and put cloths or cloth strips on the ends of the needles for more holding, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices to use one needle or two; the second suturing is common, and it is that you assemble the two keys of the skin and the two keys of the siphac together on one needle where there is strong middling thread; and when you have pierced through all these keys four together, then pull out the needle at the part where you began to sew, in the manner as one sews clothes; and leave a space between each suturing the size of a double groat; this suturing is known by men, and I stitched a wound which was on a man's belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and whose wound was over a palm large, and inside the intestines were two palms long, and whose wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I placed the intestine back into its proper place after he had been without it for 24 hours; and the wound was closed to perfection in 15 days, and I cured him, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and I put clean cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced straight through in one direction, then take the thread or suture that you have inserted the needle into, and make it pierce from the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew just as a pelter makes the furs, and you leave once the thread on one side and take it back up on the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks call properly, is such that someone does, who assemble the two parts naturally together and attach one end of the silk to the other end, in this way: take a needle or end of thread close by and make a hole only in that place, and let the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle and make a hole from the outside part just up to the inside part, at both ends of the silk; then make holes in one and the other from the outside part just up to the inside part, on two other threads that are on the other side; and this is the most correct manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this word, and anyone testifies to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one should put one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew guts; and know that when the rent is in the belly, then the stitch is more difficult than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the fire has changed it, then put back in the intestine, and the gut; then put on the powder made from burnt chalk, and if the fire has changed it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew up the edges of the flesh, and the fat; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, immediately when it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it 2 times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need another medicine in most simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound does not make common infection to the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten linen light with hot temperate oil, or rose oil, and put it around the armpits, and under the shoulders; and if it feels pain or pus in the belly, and many times happens, then cleanse them with black wine vinegar enemas, and similarly if the infection comes just to the intestine; and perforate inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is more likely to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are hurt, and this is because of the fragility of their veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach of its nature to the liquids.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the splinter springs out of the wound, so put it back in just like the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must tie the place that is black so that blood does not come out from there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and let the two ends hang down to the part under the wound as far as possible in order to lighten the extraction when the splinter falls, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can sometimes restore it in some people, because I have seen a man who was hurt with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became swollen and turned into an abscess, and from it there were vomiting and diarrhea; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtend them until they were healed, and the gut joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewed, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly; and there was no illness, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimentors said that when it has a small wound in the intestine, one should tie it in this manner: take linen from great flaxen seeds, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the linen has opened the mouth, so place it on the two lips, so that it tightens its mouth above; and then knock off the head, and it will stay so that he cannot untie it, then put another strip afterwards in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That head if it gets into the intestine, and no nuisance comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestinal thread which is very loose, and then tie at the end of this thread one thread of thin linen twisted together; then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it tight in the stitching; and this manner of sewing with strips is no further than by the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is commonly called a "fistula"; and similarly when it swells and bursts.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its true and hard white nodule formation, where one feels no pain, and it swells like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes bursts clear, and at other times thick; sometimes small, and at other times large; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is outside of only one of the nine causes: that is to say, through the thinness of blood or body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and late healing, and flees by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting that I inform you about the treatment of fistula which is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Abdominal fistules occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphac, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and such as comes to the principal property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grave sanitation, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come exactly to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to recognize it, then take a tent of lead or iron; if the fistula is straight, then search it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a subtle tent of bronze, because bronze bends more around the twistiness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, then catheterize through one of the openings, because moisture flows quickly from one opening to another, and cleans it; then search it with a cautery at your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and it is deep inside, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressing your hand on it, and where he feels it; and once you know truly where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the rottenness and the corroded flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep from a straight place, it is necessary that you cut into it, as far as you can, then put damp tents in healing medicine, and push them exactly to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments of healthy flesh so long as they are healed; and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize it just as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not bleed or hurt the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure with things that draw out flesh until it is sound; and if it is not sound, and returns to its former state, know that you are not yet gone deep enough: seek and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus sound, well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep down, so you cannot come to it; if there is no other remedy than to let nature do its thing; and if there is little corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with forceps, then draw it out with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then draw all of them out, leaving none; and if moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, then scrape and cut through the flesh and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something containing a purifying agent on the wound, and let it sit until the surrounding area around the bones is corrupted; and at that point they will be more easily moved; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then cleanse only up to the corruption until all blackness is removed, then close the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupting matter and it comes just to the edge of the bone, you must scrape and clean out everything up to the corruption, and then treat them so they are closed.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much so that the matter went to the leg and formed a large abscess; and there was no cause outside to open it. But the foolish doctors worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and they corroded a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came out many pustules that all emitted bad odor and moisture from the body; and many doctors put treatment around two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines by which they were treating him, and the matter that corroded through the pustules had a great stench; and the young man's body became red, and had yellowish-green color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of the openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one was coming against the other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the openings as far as I could see a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption had come right up to the inner bone; I removed what appeared of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except for that which I removed; and I began to treat the wound with medicinal ointments for a long time, but could not heal it; then I restarted, and saw the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to mend the place; but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and left the rest alone, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed and mended quickly, and there was no need to continue the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the evacuation blood often flowed out, but it was completely healed, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary effect whatsoever, neither to make fat nor to bring on.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, you must do it in this manner: take linen and bind it to the head of the bone which is open, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and put another piece of linen larger than the first, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, so that you draw out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the flesh at the place where you see it can be done without hurting the flesh; and put a hot iron or a wooden spatula under the bone to burn away the corrupt flesh; and you must do this until you can see and feel the corruption, and do it again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all of the flesh. Then put a hot iron underneath it, and afterwards move the sores from one side to the other, drawing out the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut through the corrupted joint and draw out the bone from the other part; and if the corruption is between two joints, then there is no other remedy than cutting. And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the wrist of the foot, it is a very serious thing, but you must always question that corrosion how it opens up to you; and cleanse it in every way that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve does not oppose you; and know that the cutting tool and the strings for cutting bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness. Therefore it is necessary to prepare each kind of instrument for every sort of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so think about the instrument that you have need of, according to what it behooves.
dou feu	of fire. (meaning that the instrument should be made of a heat-resistant material)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The body part can decay or rot either from inside or from outside; and when you have medicined the decay with the treatment of medicines, and it does not help, then you must amputate that member all the way up to where the decay comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the greater evil, which is the loss of the limb; and the sign is that the members become black, as if they had been burned with fire, and after the blackness appears, the rotting of the member will spread to all over the body; therefore hasten to amputate, and if this decay is at the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give him a moment's time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, then cut it off at the joint, so that the decay does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue; and do similarly when the decay comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut off all the foot; and if it ascends into the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy than letting the patient die; and the way of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it up above and below, and stretch out two servants one of the ties downwards, and another servant with the other tie upwards, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two ties by half a finger's breadth, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or sew, and put a linen cloth on either side, so that the stitches do not touch the healthy place, and there comes another lesion and swelling to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if hemorrhaging comes from the blood when you work, then cauterize the place quickly, or put on some restraining powders; then come back to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed. And I will tell you what happened to one man in my presence: he had a carbuncle that seemed like a fiery ember, and that ulcer came first to his knee so much that it encircled all of his leg; and when the man saw the ulcer, he hastened to cut off the leg, and was healed. And long after, the ulcer returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on things to repel the corruption of the body, but the corrosion could not cease; and he begged that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, that he would not die, for the man's virtues were weak. And he became completely despairing, and returned to his home, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed. And I have told you this story so that it might be told in turn, if one needs to do similarly.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fatty part of the body and stays so long that it makes a large gathering of pus; and then it bursts and breaks through, and the flesh comes out, just like in our skin; and the skin above is just as delicate as a loosely woven cloth, and does not reach to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches to the bone deeply, then it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut off that skin all around, and similarly when it is delicate, just like cloth; and one does not treat it for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is festering, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cut it out of a poultice thus: look to see if the breast is large, and the boil which comes from it has foul odor; then make a poultice from Egyptian medicine thus: take aloes, oil, and litharge in equal amounts, and put the mixture into an earthen vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes just as thick as honey; and then take what you need of this, and mix it with water and honey, and use it to poultice the breast, and stop up the hole; and let the medicine stay in place for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the foul odor is removed; and sometimes a poultice of ash-water is made, when this medicine is not present; and it is that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water over them, then let it drip, and use it to poultice; as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash-water, then make a poultice with honey and wine of great sweetness, for honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine makes the boil erupt; and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleansed, then make a poultice to cause flesh to grow in it, and it is that you take diaphinite ointment, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can poultice with some medicines and ointments, of which I have said the properties, and how to treat ointments; and if the hole of the boil on the breast is small, and the probe of the poultice cannot enter, then enlarge it with a piece of iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then close it up and leave only as much space as the poultice can enter into; and if the boil that pours out pus is above, then cut or lower it to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is in depth, there is no longer bleeding from it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it in such a way that the bow runs to the lowest point that it is, because when the bow is deep, there is no longer bleeding from it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it in this manner: that the bow runs lightly down, and leave nothing of the bow; and take consolidative medicines to put on the skin, and be sure on the linen cloth that covers all the skin; then cut at the strongest point the incision of the breast which is slightly larger than the first, and anoint gently on the other cloth according to the size of the incision, and put it on the incision of the breast to loosen the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside that once after many days; and the one who is on the incision of the breast, take often to remove the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it's venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that appears on the incision of the breast, know that the breast is healing already, and approach health; and then release it in the morning, or the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is discharging undigested pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons corrupt after a long time, then do not despair of health, for the patient is approaching recovery.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly with pus in their sores, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested flesh jumps out of the chest after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast takes a long time to close up, and is swollen, then add moist and dry medicines in substance and virtue, such as diaphanous ointment, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take diaphanous ointment and make with rose oil and equal vine wine; then boil it and use it; and do the same thing when clematis honey is thickened, or you take myrrh, aloes, and incense, and grind them, and powder on the honey when it is on the fire; and then apply it to a cloth and bind it on the breast, and sometimes administer a long aristologe, and roots of celestial lily, which are also like flour of verjuice and centaury; and use simples or composites: grind them up and make powder, and put on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is drawn out and is not healed by this cure, then know that corruption has penetrated deeply and made an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so apply the treatment for fistulae, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the swelling (apostème) of the navel.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it becomes old, and one takes no care, then the abscess bursts forth, and runs and flows downwards until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps even runs all the way through; and comes the corrosion just to the bone, so that there is a foul pain, and the joint of the toe is wide open, and the color is darkened.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you cut off from it all the remaining superfluity which is left of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; but if the nail presses into the flesh, begins to prick and bleed, then it is necessary that you put a hot iron under the nail which pricks the flesh, and lift it up, and cut off that subtle and delicate flesh, and apply on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines in order to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the ulcer is in the bone, then cut it out and remove all that's corrupted, for as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal; and if you see that the two bones are corroding, then cut them apart just as was said before, then cure them until they're healed; and if it's been pierced, and you've inserted something in it, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first; then cut out the splinter with a cross-cutting knife above, and be careful that the blade does not reach to the flesh under the splinter, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then place something on top which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the deafness or numbness of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The tendons that arise in the hands of certain people by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a piece where they have bones, and sometimes there is an angle, and some of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the tendons.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born without any deformity of the knee cannot move it; and those who are born with a deformity of the joint of the knee may be able to move it; the length of that person is slight, in the same way: let them stretch out their legs from the root of a large sparrow's wing.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, is hard to cure: you must hold on to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born with or have a swelling at the back of the knee, it is necessary that you cut off the flesh all around to the bone first, then cut the bone to a suitable thread; then cure them until they are healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the feet together are caused by birth, or by a blow from an accident, or by being burned with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut open the sewn-up part, so that it may be repaired according to its natural form; then put between two tents or moistened linen cloths in rose oil, so that they do not become stuck together; or put between two thin slices of dough until the place is sewn up, as needs to be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes to any part of his foot with the palm (of his hand), then cut out the swelling in the way that is necessary.
des vils	From evil places
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are swollen, inflated and filled with melancholic superfluities that come to many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer them an occasional purging with senna, and then heal the boil with the help of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of the vein is in two ways: one way is to cut it, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and drain all its flow.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this way: first raise the leg with a very hot iron point until the thick blood is thinned out, then strain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, with a large incision, then lift and drain out the black blood by hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate; and then bind it, and instruct him that he should eat savory foods, such as dark red broth; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The limb of the patient is cleansed according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient if it has much hair, then place it in a bath, and rub the leg with hot water until it becomes red and inflamed; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then tie a long piece of linen cloth around the vein at the knee or on the part below the ankle; then open the skin to the length of the vessel, and peel off the vein from each side until one feels it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then place the string underneath, so that it is elevated from the skin, and then tie it lightly to the linen cloth, then tie another length in another place three times; then peel off the skin on top of the vein until it is felt, then lift it up as you have done, and tie it to another linen cloth as you have done first; then tie a third length, or more if necessary, then lift it up, and tie it to the two ends of the foot; then pull and lift it just like the second length; then pull it out from length to length until it is completely free, then tie it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, place a needle in all the strong double thread, and tie and pull, and place underneath the string, and turn your hand from one side and the other until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, for if it cuts, then one will not be able to pull or lift it, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have completely pulled it out, place some moist linen on top of the wound in vinegar and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and tangled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, so you must cut it askew, but do not close it; and handle it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one closes the vein is curved, and does not cut, so as to close the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were subtle, one would pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry earth; and it may also be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from under the skin, just as snakes and worms come inside the body, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	If the signs of the beginning of this vein soth are that it comes in the leg a great inflammation; then it changes its place and begins to come out as if it were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein bursts open, you must wrap around it a piece of cloth from one to two ells and a half up to II ells, and a thread; and let the cloth stay on the leg, and every time its end points outside, then wrap around the cloth and the thread; and if it is too long, then cut off part of it, and wrap the remaining part around it, and do not cut it in its root until it is entirely out; because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction at the place, and a bad illness; for this reason it must be treated little by little up to the end, and nothing should remain in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated up to five palms long, or up to ten, and one came to me once, from whom it issued up to ten palms long, and when you cut it, the flesh bursts out or a hole forms, and the place becomes empty, and medicine for purging putrefaction every day cures it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And every time to this wound there are many discharges, and indeed when it bursts in the joint of the foot, or the foot, and there is a great deal of pus, and from which he jumps up with discharges; then treat him thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "the disease of an ox", because it has happened many times to the oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and it feels so badly from limb to limb, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and jumps out; and it arises from some corruption of humors, such as come worms and serpents and lice and tape worms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance entering, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and cleansed, one cannot avoid the pain as soon as it moves: so you must bind its place above and below with a strong thread tightly; then strike upwards and cleanse it thoroughly, and if the abscess is deeply rooted in the flesh, and you do not find it, scorch it with fire on top until it suppurates; and the greatest harm it does is that it causes the eye to run, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head near the eye, then press firmly underneath it the eyelid, then strike upwards, and cleanse it thoroughly; and the patient must be treated with cleansing of the body of soluble medicines for bad humors, and beware of rotten foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to an ailing woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I looked again, and I saw it rising just like a worm on the shoulder, as quickly as sharp silver when it comes out of its place; the pain departed from that place, and lodged itself in the shoulder, and then shortly afterwards coursed all through the body until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she was constantly turning around her body, just like I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease move in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had often seen that it was well to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not see this in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason the constraint appeared to me; and they did not appear to be according to this reason in those who are sluggish, and who have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then bind above and below hastily; and then strike above so that that swelling is constrained back into place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it to yourself, then cure with those who expel swellings, such as fetid pills, and serpent pilules, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kinds is that there are those with great points, and small ones, and hooked ones, and pointed ones; and those with two edges, and those with shafts, and those with pieces; and the one that lodges in any member so lodges in two manners: or it pierces a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, becomes apparent: so you should beware of the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this ill sign does not become apparent to you, and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.
