And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and bursts the skull above the brain, is when there is scotoma and stupor and convulsion and confusion in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixing up of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps also there is a discharge from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps the word and voice are lost; and there is a wet white wound like a blister, and it bursts also like a boil; and if this sign becomes apparent to you, then beware of the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it pierces the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves as the hair does, and there is dark bleeding, and a chill and cold sweat, and fainting: you should then be without doubt that the person will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter that never lets the lung be is that without pain it bursts forth from the wound with a foam-like discharge, and the throat swells, and the sick person's face changes color, and gasps loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter falls on the covering of the ribcage, it is located near the small ribs; and it brings great pain and great suffering and gasping; and it moves all the muscles of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls on the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat will burst out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter falls on the belly and bursts through the intestine's outlet, then there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the splinter falls on the bladder and the urine bursts out and comes forth, and the sick person feels very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and neck and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and ribcage and chest and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or artery and it's not venomous, just as I will tell you how it happened to me, because you may do something similar.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow pierced the eyelid near the root of the nose: I tried it and pulled it out from the other side under the fatty part of the ear, and he was healed without suffering.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had pierced the fatty part of the eye under the eyebrow: and the arrow was bent back and I could only grasp the tip towards the bowstring, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron without any ears; the boy was healed, and no bad outcome came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab in origin with golden tips; I smoothed out the fletching, and sharpened it until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew out an arrow from the side of a man who had been struck in the belly, and I thought he was dying; and after 30 days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow and extracted it, and pulled it out, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow fell on a man's back, and the wound was sewn up over it; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural disposition, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural activities.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow had fallen in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And draw out an arrow from the body of the prince, king, who it was stuck in the navel, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for 3 days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with a thin needle and did not feel anything; and he felt pain and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on the place ointment atractif and digestive, so that the wound would not swell; and the appearance of the place of the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the ointment again for many days, and the wound healed once more, and the patient remained thus a long time, until he felt the arrow one day within his navel; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied medicine with corrosive properties by hand for many days until the wound was open; and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrowhead which was rusting at its base; then I inserted into the opening of the wound that medicine with corrode, until the tip of the arrowhead became visible to me; and passed well over four months, and then broke out so much from the wound that I put in forceps, and drew it from both sides, and could not come out; then I ceased not to subtilize and ingenier by manners of instruments, until I caught it one day with fine forceps, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I caught and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sown together, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may put your treatment on what I do not say; for a book cannot take up everything; but wise masters gather well about little things, and about those which are present and deficient, find new work, and new instrument, to deal with strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from limbs or where they are stuck except in two manners: either through the place where they enter, or otherwise; and that which jumps out from the place where it enters, is an arrow entering fleshly parts, and this happens sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, so let it remain until the flesh is rotting around it, and the issue becomes clean; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, so let it be left thus for some days, and each day move it; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, so pierce around it with a very fine instrument, until the place around it is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and among the accidents that I have said, advise the patient: do not pull it out at all, but let it be so long as it is equal after some days, because if the arrow reaches such a depth, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach such depth, and the patient remains for some days without a bad accident, then you should take out the instrument of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she is very stuck in like that and cannot come out, then administer theriacs around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is replaced in its place in the body so that you cannot see it, search for it everywhere; and if you feel it, take out the instrument of pulling with it. And if you can't because of the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there's no bone or nerve or vein, then cut around the wound as much as it will be large. Take out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is lodged in two parts up to the place where you can see, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you hurt yourself more.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the area around the wound is rotten, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be facilitated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and devise how you may draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the shape he was when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, if it pierces any part of him, or the skin is swollen in front where you can see it or feel it apparently: cut then upwards, so long as the forceps can catch hold, and then pull it out: if it springs forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round so that it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again and start pulling out again as long as it comes forth; and if the head of the arrow is in it, so insert the whole shaft; and if the shaft slips, and you see that you can administer oil, then administer an instrument with a groove, such that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forth, and if the arrow is stuck, then insert the instrument with a pointed end in, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, then it behooves you to cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, and then treat the wound as seems fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow lies in the chest or belly or bladder or ribcage and is nearby and you can cut on it, so cut; but guard against cutting into the vein and nerve, and then pull out the arrow, and then cut the wound, as seems necessary; and cure until it is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to remove awls are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here their form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the awl.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, to put on the tip of the arrow, such as this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and knowing whether [the awl] is there or not is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	sharp points of common pincers.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins for cleansing with which one saves oneself, of which there is sixteen in the head, namely: two blood vessels that are after the ears, called "herbech"; and two arteries that appear in both temples; and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the neck; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bloodletting are V-shaped in each arm: the one is the cephalic, and is located on the left side; and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fistula", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side; and the common people call it "vein of the belly"; and it is above the elbow, and it is that one from which we bleed, which appears manifestly on the bicep.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the bend of the knee on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "saphenous" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears is said to aid against catharsis and migraine; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, and scrub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a screw until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places from the head: which is to be done by both hands, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, sign that it is ready; then take the lancet, and thrust it through the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein up, and cut and bleed the skin and vein very well two do's of length, and make the blood come out as much as you see; then bind and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth to bleed an elderly person, and old, and habitual, and accustomed to eye problems, and in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is such as I say: that the patient strains his neck so much that the two veins appear openly; and feels the spot under your thumb's nail, then signals to bleed; then lift the lancet over the vein high up on your index finger, and plunge it down, and lift the vein high, and cut it, just as you have done in the other two veins, and make the bleeding stop according to your need; then let the patient go, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then tie it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have also spoken of their closure and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein in front of the head is worth as much as the bleeding from the cerebral vein in ancient diseases and migraines, and headaches; and its quality is that the patient twists his neck so tightly that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point of the instrument above the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let two veins flow according to what you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein so that it is tied up and at no time is a wide incision made.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not suitable that the bandages be too tight; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close, and perhaps break the bandages when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the eyelids helps eyes and the mange, and headaches, and the oriuel in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient twists his neck tightly with some thread, as before; then let it bleed, and the wound should be a cut across, a little long and a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is thin, it might break; then make a new one from blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the neck is worth a lot against ague and sudden fever, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens their throat, then holds their neck with your left hand, and takes the subtle flame long, and puts it inside the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to flow now; and do not go too deep at first, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two sinewy veins is helpful against the tightening of the arm, and the beginning of putrefaction, and many diseases, and swelling, and corrosion, and herpes, and itching; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens their neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master should be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient should sit on a seat, then let out the vein of long a little widely, then draw the blood temperately, or as long as is necessary; then do it again in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and hold both veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave him until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting from the veins of the upper lips is helpful for swelling in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cuts or splits of the lips, and of the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the venesection are that you have the patient sit in front of you, and bind their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and you recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black spots: cut both, and if you do not know them, and you have doubt, then cut the larger one from each side; and so do with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the venesection under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The venesection under the tongue helps after the venesection of the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the one who performs this are that the patient sits in your hands before the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein: then cut both, and do not go too deeply, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut from which one commonly bleeds are healed according to two manners: or they prick all in a wide flamelet made of myrrh, or an olive leaf so fine as surgeon's knives are; and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the thin bandage is very well-known, and it's wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening the veins with clear blood and apparent large blood and turmoil; and this is the form of olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is sharper pointed, and is for bleeding the small veins in which there is clear yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him skillfully, and to warn off the artery that lies below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes pouring out, then he must stop it, as I said; and the flame should not be pricked, but cut like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open visibly, then you must draw it out, and change to another one; or you want to let some liquid from it, or you cure with wine in place of it in the arm: it opens visibly; and the swelling goes down with a burn, just as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm, so that you touch the location until you know the pulse; then mark the location of the incision, and then bind the arm, and heat the vein with a burn; and beware that you do not hit in the artery when you see the location swollen, for it is of the artery: then withdraw.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out above as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood of the artery: hasten then, and put your thumb on top for a long time, then take away your thumb if the bleeding stops, which happens many times; bind up the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding doesn't stop and it's bothering you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens up, because the head will retreat; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a peel of fig tree and boil it, and take one half and bind well just up to the other edge; if the blood is stopped, that's well; if not, cure with the powders that stop blood; and the clotting is not hard in most dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the tendon of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wine of the vein in vinegar is so helpful that it treats blood flowing from the top of the head and from the belly, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to be careful for the nerve which is below, and if he pierces too deep and finds the nerve, it swells up and the wound becomes hard, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often shows itself, and if it does not show itself in some men because of its subtlety, then you must use the cauterizing instrument on the vein; and push the nerve with all your might.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment of the cephalic vein is so helpful that it attracts blood from the head and helps the eyes; and one must bleed with a burning olive branch or a burning myrtle twig, for this is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Anyway, one must find the lightest place, and not harm anything if it is missed the first time, and try again; and it happens that the places are swollen in some men when it is missed the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bloodletting is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done except to preserve health and to prevent diseases from coming; and the bleeding is done in one of the three veins that are in front: that is to say, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic; and one must bleed at the beginning of winter, and in autumn and in summer after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who tends to the sick has no certain cure, but when need arises day or night in all hours and times; and it is not necessary to heal children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child for more than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should elderly people who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they defecate with a light enema if they have retained much bad humors, so that the veins do not draw out bad substances from the intestines and harm the main members; nor does one heal who is too full of meat, or drunk until he has recovered, or dropsy; and if one tries to heal after a colic passion, vomiting, and defecation of the belly, and multiple visits by women, and labor, watching and rising, and all things that take away virtue, either from an armed wound or from the body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and heal the vein of the belly around the third part, as we have said; and keep that day free from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyful, and let the physician be higher than him whom one heals, and wipe the arm twice or three times, then loosen the string above gradually, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then wipe the physician's hands on the place where one wants to heal, until the veins swell and one can feel them; then moisten the physician's hands with the flame of a little old oil, then put his right hand on top of that vein under the place where one wants to heal, so that the vein does not become inflamed and burst from the piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow like strings to be cut out by the surgeon, and there are such ones that are full of windiness, so that when you put on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and similarly is one; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the surgeon to be skilled in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts at first attempt, that's good; but if not, then try again a little below or above that place with more haste, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed, and the patient fears, let him leave it for a day or two, and do not tie his arm: perhaps there will come abscesses that are warm; nor enter into a bath, then resume the treatment if he likes; and if the wound is small, cut out the blood carefully and you doubt that it may not bleed as much as you see, so believe in the same wound itself with all the flame straightly; and do some work hastily, thus while the swelling is inflamed; for these things have happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not start to lance it again, and put a little bit of linseed oil on it, because it makes the body light in blood, and the oil is mixed with the lymph that is in this place; and thus administer the linseed oil in each lance that you lance veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same thing for treacle and poultice when you put them on the place; so subtly clean the pus and it will break up when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes that has been many times, especially when it is not fully cured this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a wet sponge on the place in hot water and vinegar for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein stops, and if there remains some discoloration or greenish color at the place after some days, it does not harm him; and if you see fit, put something made of aloes or myrrh that has been soaked in camphor, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times it has happened that there is an swelling and appearance at the time of bloodletting from the basilic vein: then put your hand on top of it, and if you feel the place soft to the compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Withdraw then, and do not put anything on it of what we have said, because perhaps the bleeding will cut an artery; but make one dry poultice to harden the place, then apply another treatment, until they are healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood separately according to its quantity of virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see a lot of it, let it flow out until it thins out; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is swollen and full of blood and needs extraction of blood, to make a wider wound and have the flaps wide; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and need to be healed quickly and often, and should be healed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing preserves against bleeding of blood and damaging of nerves, and is better than the long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body fails at healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in juice of green apples; if he is overheated, then bleed him three or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, then moisten bread before healing with sweet syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he spits up at the sainie, after the issue of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks a broth made from meat, and a sweet-smelling syrup, and uses the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to shake off his arm and recover another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed a little at a time, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to shake off his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong veins, then he bleeds .vii (seven) hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another part, then he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has much blood inside the body that is already heated up, and makes fever come; so it is necessary to drain a great quantity, and to enlarge the vein as far as it can be opened; then you reward all the conditions of sainie, and put your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, lest death should come in place of paresis, and this happens many times when the nurse is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see the arm untied, and blood issuing the second time, and the vein closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is curved, to straighten the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds again the second time; or you point at him with a flame's point, as far as the frozen blood issues through the vein's opening, and put on a small pouch of thread soaked in water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then leave it alone and do not constrict it again, until the swelling has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing out blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled instead of the neck vein because it is more composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The manner of the surgery is thus: the patient puts his hand in hot water until the scab is red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well; then the scab should be cut through now, not through width or length; and the incision should be large, and the wound should be made clean right next to the joint of the hand, and if there's no bleeding, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood congeal in the water as much as you have; and if it's winter, do not put the hand in hot water again, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and this vein is safe from all other veins, with no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The surgery on the liver vein of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: straining the hand, and putting it in hot water until the wound is closed, so that you can see it; and if the scab cuts through, and you cut away everything completely, then nothing will hurt; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are under all bare of flesh, and put the hand back in hot water, if the blood congeals in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out blood as much as is necessary for you, then put on the vein oil and string to close it quickly, and so do with each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cut in the left hand is worth a disease of epilepsy, and do all alike as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The patient with dropsy is considered to be sick in all the diseases that are under the skin, such as diseases of the kidneys and retention of fluids, and disease of the reins, and of the knees and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his disease is that the patient puts their foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein as long as it breaks open, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many bad humors; therefore treat the most swollen one, or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it on the foot, you will go towards the nerves that are under, and the cut of crossing as when cutting; and the wound should be old.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the treatment fails the first time, then try it again the second time above a pot, for the place is salty; nor doubt about nerves, as we have said, and thus treat the disease of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the back leg, and its cut is worth the pain of the haunch, when it's for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient enters into it and applies it above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then he cleans it with all manner of cleansing that you can, and crossing over; and it is worth noting that you must close it, for the place is clean, and it has been repented by many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not see it, then clean the vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and watch out for nerves; and stop as much blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	ventouse salves
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Vacuum cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and vacuum therapy is done in two ways: either by cutting and attracting blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventouse treatment which is without piercing is in two manners: or it is on fire at all times, or not; and the ventouse made by piercing and bloodletting is done in fourteen places of the body, from which one is entirely on the head; and the other is in the neck; and two others are in the two sides of the neck; and the ventouse under the chin; and the ventouse over the shoulders; and the ventouses in the two hips; and the ventouses in the two arms; and the ventouses in the two legs; and the ventouses on the two ankles; and this treatment does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it has not weakened anyone at all, as one does with a vein cleansing treatment; and it must not be administered, nor at all times, nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessities of illnesses it becomes necessary to bleed, or because of habits, we should lead them each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between and in each time; for there are such who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and those who find repletion and redness in their face, and on their head, and on the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and shed blood; and there are such who dream, and see through fresh blood and hurt and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, let us order them to be vacuumed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding from the nose helps with the congestion of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this bleeding is in place of the bloodletting from the cerebral vein, and it is not necessary for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have catharrhea, because this does great harm to them; and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become forgetful, and because of this, it is suitable to place the poultice a bit lower by the forehead's part of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vapour bath near the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it is good for constriction of the belly, and for breaking of the channel of the womb, and for tonsils, and for repletion; and it should be placed beneath, for if it holds too tightly, it causes vomiting or nausea and the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vapour baths in two places of the neck are good for pains of the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the sinew of the basilic vein; and you should command the surgeon that he stretches his hand to put [it] on, so that he does not touch the artery, and does not let go of blood prematurely.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The inflamations under the chin are worth the diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and they replace the healthy flesh of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflamations on the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The vapour baths of the sides are as good as the three veins of the arm, because they attract blood from these thick veins; and command the surgeon that he should not pierce too far in depth, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies over nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is above the buttocks is worth as much as hemorrhoids of the fundament and illnesses below, and it is necessary that the poultice be big and made of lead, so that it can draw well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break through; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The poultices on the legs are clearly curative, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth as much as old pains in the kidneys, gallbladder, and bladder, and they help to remove boils; and they replace the two shins and the two ankles, and nonetheless, they weaken the body after long use, and bring on a condition of paleness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the poultice is that you first put it on empty, and then immediately squeeze out the air, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and you appear the redness of the blood; then strike [the area], and reapply the poultices, and take note of the body's disposition, for there are some who have too much flesh, and clear pores: if it is necessary to hit only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a bit deep; and squeeze lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike two times: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out little by little, piece by piece, then we suffice with only one [strike].
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, so often do we recommend it; and if the blood is thick, we pierce in depth, and the ends so are that the kidneys be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for him who has hard skin and rough, and who have large pores, that you grease the places of the venuouses with dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with oil from melon seeds; and if it is in winter, with nettle oil, or with lily oil, or with chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom we bleed has tender skin and large pores, there is no need to put oil on it, but rather it should be washed after bleeding with rose water, or cold water, or hawthorn water, or melon water, or porcelain berry water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has too much moisture, should get up with ease, or with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive swelling should get up from old wine, or vinegar of apple cider, or a decoction of mint or chamomile, or similar things; and it is not necessary to heal with a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and he must wake up when he should be poulted and when he has been pouted.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are choleric in their health, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed; so it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things; and pomegranate juice, and mutton fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, so they take honey syrup and aromatic wine that is between old and new, and pomegranate juice, and pomegranate juice and small birds such as pigeons; and the day he will be poulticed, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men at one time treacle or muscade before the poultice, or after, to comfort the main members; and thin the blood, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are put to cause bleeding are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and on gout, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the hip, for those members cannot bear being struck there, and one only does so to attract blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the woman bleeds; in order to remove viscosity that is on the member, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the navel to reduce the size of the member; and to take away pain, when there is swelling or stone, it takes away by its attracting virtue perhaps the swelling, or loosens the stone from its place; and thus it does it when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty so that they suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of hot broth, as in diseases of the eye, and in such a way one fills the cup with warm water alone, or with water that has cooked herbs which are beneficial for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered at fire, thus is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be 2 inches and a half palm deep, and there should be on the edge around the middle a small perforation, as to stick in a needle, and of brass, soft before so that it does not hurt the patient when putting on the limb; and there should be in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron to put a candle in place, and they should be great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for children's poultices are other than old people's, and thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should put this poultice on the limb: take a candle of wax or linen cloth, and put it in the middle of the poultice at the end of the crossbar that is in the poultice, so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and you should have it be over the perforation that we said, so that when one wants to, if there are vapors, they go out, and take off the poultice; and apply the cloth as before, and do it again often, if need be.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse that is administered for the illness of pleurisy, it has no spike or point, and is not applied except when it is full of water, and is placed on the member as such; and this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.
